# Clem Feedback E2E Execution Contract

**Owner**: /Users/arimendelow/Projects/spoonjoy-v2-clem-feedback/worker/tasks/2026-07-14-1313-doing-clem-feedback-e2e/EXECUTION-CONTRACT.md
**Planning**: ../2026-07-14-1313-planning-clem-feedback-e2e.md
**Doing**: ../2026-07-14-1313-doing-clem-feedback-e2e.md
**Status**: reviewer-gated

This doing-owned artifact is the sole exact technical authority for schemas, CLI vectors, storage bytes, ordering, crash recovery, and terminal protocols. Planning retains product and architecture decisions only. The doing units implement and verify this contract without inventing behavior.


**Shopping-List State Matrix**

| Existing row | Quantity after add | Checked state | Ordering | Category/icon |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| No row | Requested quantity exactly, including `null` | Unchecked; `checkedAt` and `deletedAt` null | Newly allocated end position | Per field, explicit string or null stores exactly; omitted infers from ingredient name through `resolveIngredientAffordance` |
| Active, unchecked | If requested is `null`, retain existing; otherwise `(existing ?? 0) + requested` | Unchecked | Unchanged | Preserve unless request explicitly overrides |
| Active, checked | If requested is `null`, retain existing; otherwise `(existing ?? 0) + requested` | Reset unchecked; clear `checkedAt` | Move to a newly allocated end position | Preserve unless request explicitly overrides |
| Deleted tombstone | Requested quantity exactly, including `null`; never add stale quantity | Reset unchecked; clear `checkedAt` and `deletedAt` | Move to a newly allocated end position | Per field, explicit string or null stores exactly; omitted preserves stored non-null and infers only stored-null through `resolveIngredientAffordance` |

Recipe batch adds aggregate equal ingredient-reference/unit pairs before mutation: numeric requested quantities sum, while an all-null group remains null. Web, REST, and MCP call the same D1-safe helper.

Every post-migration active item obeys `checked === (checkedAt !== null)`. Other item commands are exact: setting an unchecked active item checked captures the batch timestamp, sets both fields, and moves it to one newly allocated end slot; setting a checked active item unchecked clears both fields and preserves sortIndex; requesting the already-canonical state is a no-op. Single delete preserves item content/order/check fields and sets deletedAt on an active item; an already-deleted target is a no-op. Clear-completed applies that delete transition to every active checked item; clear-all applies it to every active item. Deletes never compact or rewrite surviving sortIndex values. An empty aggregate, missing eligible target, or clear with zero eligible rows changes no row, version, allocator, or timestamp. The old `normalizeShoppingListOrdering` write path is removed rather than treated as a reorder command; this release adds no user reorder API.

All content-changing shopping-list commands use an atomic list-level lease/version batch. `ShoppingList` adds `mutationVersion Int @default(0)`, nullable `mutationLease String?`, and `nextSortIndex Int @default(0)`. Empty aggregate add, set-checked/delete against a missing list/target, and clear against a missing/empty list return no-op before any list INSERT. Only a fully validated add/free-text/recipe aggregate with at least one row that can create or restore content may bootstrap. It uses one parameterized `INSERT ... ON CONFLICT(authorId) DO NOTHING` with a caller-generated nonempty id, version/index zero, null lease, and database timestamps; concurrent losers read the winner, and bootstrap itself never creates an item or consumes version/index. Every attempt reads that ShoppingList row/version `V` first, then its item snapshot sequentially. It computes the exact changed set/reserved count and returns immediately for a no-op. Otherwise one non-interactive D1 transaction conditionally acquires a random lowercase UUID-v4 lease only where `mutationVersion = V AND mutationLease IS NULL`, guards every item statement and contiguous allocation on that lease, then clears the lease and increments version. A concurrent commit visible during or after item read makes the version CAS fail, every guarded statement no-op, and the request retry from a fresh version-first read. Eight attempts use fixed inter-attempt delays 5, 10, 20, 40, 80, 160, and 320 ms; exhaustion throws `ShoppingListBusyError`. REST maps it to additive `409 write_conflict` / `Shopping list changed too frequently; retry.`, web returns that message with 409, and MCP returns a retryable tool error with that text. Every add/set-checked/delete/clear web, v1, MCP, and recipe writer uses this coordinator.

Equal ingredient-reference/unit pairs aggregate in original request order. Numeric quantities sum and an all-null group stays null. Category/icon use independent three-state input. Explicit string or null always stores exactly; the last explicit aggregate value per field wins. Omitted on an active row preserves that field even when null. Omitted on a missing row infers that field from canonical ingredient name through `resolveIngredientAffordance`. Omitted on a tombstone preserves a stored non-null field but infers only a stored-null field; it never recomputes a non-null tombstone affordance. The accepted item batch is all-or-nothing. `nextSortIndex` reserves one contiguous range in aggregate input order; abort/retry never consumes it. Successful check/add/restore moves and deletes may leave gaps. Concurrent numeric adds sum, null adds retain serialization-current quantity, simultaneous tombstone restores become first restore plus subsequent active add, and later commit wins conflicting overrides; tests force both D1 commit orders.

One accepted content-changing batch captures one safe `acceptedAtMs = max(platformNowMs, ShoppingList.updatedAtMs + 1, each changed existing item's updatedAtMs + 1)` before SQL and range-checks it against the JavaScript Date limit. Every created/changed item and the parent ShoppingList receive exactly its canonical ISO timestamp; untouched rows do not. A no-op, failed capacity check, lost lease, aborted transaction, or retry changes no timestamp. This monotonic list clock makes REST/native sync cursors observe every accepted mutation even when multiple changed items share a timestamp; item-id tie order remains authoritative inside one batch.

Nullable-unit identity is database-enforced without a sentinel collision. Migration 0024 groups by actual `(shoppingListId, ingredientRefId, unitId)` so SQL NULLs group together; the existing Prisma composite unique continues to protect non-null unit IDs, and exact partial unique index `ShoppingListItem_list_ingredient_null_unit_key` protects `(shoppingListId, ingredientRefId) WHERE unitId IS NULL`. Before reconciliation it normalizes every legacy row by canonical checked value `checked OR checkedAt IS NOT NULL`: false/null stays unchecked; false/non-null becomes checked preserving checkedAt; true/non-null remains; true/null becomes checked with checkedAt=updatedAt. Within each duplicate group order is active before tombstoned, then sortIndex, updatedAt, id. If active rows exist, the first is survivor; its quantity is the finite sum of active non-null quantities or null when all are null, it is active, it is unchecked/null if any active row is canonical-unchecked, otherwise checked with the first active checkedAt in order, and category/icon are the first non-null active values in order. If all are tombstones, the first normalized row survives unchanged. Every nonsurvivor is deleted.

Migration 0024 creates durable `ShoppingListItemSyncTombstone` before reconciliation so deleting a duplicate never creates a client-side ghost. Its exact no-extra-purpose row is the original loser id plus `shoppingListId`, preserved normalized `quantity`, `unitName`, `ingredientName`, `checked`, `checkedAt`, `sortIndex`, `categoryKey`, and `iconKey`, with `deletedAt` equal to the loser's existing deletion time or the account's migrationSyncAt for an active loser, and `updatedAt` equal to migrationSyncAt. It has a cascading ShoppingList relation, primary key `id`, and cursor index `(shoppingListId,updatedAt,id)`. Before any write, migration 0024 captures one database-now millisecond and computes per affected account/list `syncHighWaterMs` as the exact maximum of that value and every timestamp that either pre-migration sync endpoint can issue in a cursor: `User.updatedAt`, `ShoppingList.updatedAt`, every ShoppingListItem.updatedAt, every active Recipe.updatedAt, every Cookbook.updatedAt, and every NativeSyncTombstone.updatedAt for the author. Every source timestamp must parse to a canonical finite JavaScript-Date millisecond. Exact `migrationSyncAtMs=syncHighWaterMs+1` must remain within the JavaScript Date limit; parse/range/overflow failure aborts the whole migration before schema/data writes. This dominates equal and future-skewed stored timestamps from both shopping and native account streams, including a native cursor last advanced by another resource kind. The migration copies every nonsurvivor into the ledger before hard deletion, and rerun neither duplicates nor retimestamps a row. `GET /api/v1/shopping-list/sync` merges live/soft-deleted items with these ledger rows, maps a ledger row to the existing deleted shopping-item payload, and orders/pages the combined stream by `(updatedAt,id)`. `GET /api/v1/me/sync` merges the same ledger rows as `action:'delete',kind:'shoppingItem'` with exact parent/title/deletion metadata and its existing `(updatedAt,kind,id)` cursor order. Ordinary shopping-list reads exclude the ledger. Route tests prove legacy ISO and opaque composite cursors at the former high-water timestamp, tied ids on either side of the cursor, and a native cursor advanced by a future-skewed profile/recipe/cookbook/tombstone all receive every deleted duplicate id through both sync APIs; a cursor at migrationSyncAt does not replay them, pagination neither drops nor duplicates an id, rerun preserves cursor bytes/timestamps, and user/list deletion cascades the ledger.

Before any migration write, SQL guards prove the sync high-water/date rules above, every existing sortIndex is an integer in `0..2_147_483_646`, and every non-null duplicate active-quantity sum is finite and in `[-Number.MAX_VALUE, Number.MAX_VALUE]`; failure rolls back the whole D1 migration and leaves original rows/schema. `nextSortIndex` initializes to zero for empty lists or exact widened `MAX(sortIndex)+1` otherwise, so `2_147_483_647` is the exhausted sentinel and never an item sortIndex. Reconciled survivors, every new loser tombstone, and parent lists get that account's exact migrationSyncAt so both cursor streams see all changes. Migration rerun is harmless.

Three-state inputs are exact before aggregation. REST JSON and MCP: absent/`undefined` means omitted, JSON/tool `null` means explicit null, and any string including `""` means that exact explicit string; other types and unknown fields are validation errors. Web FormData: zero entries means omitted, exactly one string entry including `""` is explicit, a File or repeated field is `400`; literal `null` is a string. Recipe ingredient batches and free-text creation pass omitted affordances after canonical ingredient-name resolution. Quantity inputs/results must be finite and in `[-Number.MAX_VALUE, Number.MAX_VALUE]`; overflow maps to exact `Quantity is outside supported numeric range.` Global IngredientRef/Unit get-or-create happens idempotently before the list transaction and is explicitly outside item-batch atomicity: a later busy/capacity failure may leave an unreferenced canonical dictionary row but never partial user/list state.

Shopping `mutationVersion`/`nextSortIndex` are `0..2_147_483_647`; item sortIndex is `0..2_147_483_646`. A content change requires `mutationVersion < 2_147_483_647`, every retained sortIndex in range, and widened `nextSortIndex + reservedCount <= 2_147_483_647`; allocated indexes are `[nextSortIndex,nextSortIndex+reservedCount-1]`, then the stored next value advances by reservedCount. Thus allocating index `2_147_483_646` legally stores the exhausted sentinel, and any later allocation fails without writes. Capacity failure throws `ShoppingListCapacityError`; REST returns `409 capacity_exceeded` / `Shopping list numeric capacity reached.`, web returns 409 with that message, and MCP returns a non-retryable tool error. Lease retries never mask capacity/quantity errors.

**Cook-Session Ownership And Lifecycle**
- Every non-101 cook response carries `X-Request-Id`. JSON success is `{ ok: true, requestId, data }`; JSON error is `{ ok: false, requestId, error: { code, message, status }, data? }`. Exact `stale_attempt`, `stale_revision`, and `session_purging` errors occur only while a current snapshot exists and require `data:{snapshot}` equal to that current state; every other error forbids `data`. A bodyless 204 still carries `X-Request-Id`, `Cache-Control: private, no-store`, and `Pragma: no-cache` but no envelope/body. An inbound trimmed `X-Request-Id` matching `^[A-Za-z0-9._:-]{1,128}$` is echoed; otherwise generate `req_<lowercase UUID-v4>`. The response header and envelope value are identical. Every other non-101 response has the same private headers.
- `POST /api/cook-sessions` accepts exact JSON `{ recipeId, mutationId, adoption? }`; unknown fields and explicit `adoption: null` are 422. `adoption`, when present, is exactly `{ version: 1, recipeFingerprint, activeStepIndex, scaleFactor, checkedIngredientIds, checkedStepOutputIds }`; local anonymous `updatedAt` is never transmitted, accepted, or hashed. The persisted start command stores `adoption: AdoptionInput|null`; null encodes wire omission. A newly accepted create returns 201; an ACTIVE resume with a fresh mutation returns 200; an exact live replay returns its recorded 200/201 status and adoptionOutcome but always the current evolved snapshot while its attempt remains current. The ledger's accepted snapshot is audit/recovery evidence only, never live replay response content. Data is `{ snapshot, adoptionOutcome }` with exact `not_requested|adopted|server_won`. Absent adoption is `not_requested`. Every supplied object first requires exact fields/version, recipeFingerprint matching `^[0-9a-f]{64}$` without normalization, safe-integer index, finite scale 0.25..50, and nonempty-string duplicate-free arrays; structural failure returns 422 before state lookup. Pristine first start also requires current fingerprint/index/subsets; applied state arrays are canonicalized in pinned traversal order, success is `adopted`, and semantic failure is 422. Permanent content-free `history:v1` decides pristine: only its absence permits adoption, and the first accepted attempt atomically creates it. With history present, structurally valid adoption is ignored without recipe/pinned identity comparison and returns `server_won`, even after all attempts/coordinator/tombstones expire. Idempotency canonicalization is state-independent and defined below. The separate 64-entry/24-hour replay/conflict/tombstone/backpressure rules remain.
- Composite identity uses one injective component function everywhere. For a nonempty JavaScript string id, `storageIdComponent(id)` is unpadded base64url of UTF-8 bytes of exact `JSON.stringify(id)`; JSON escaping makes lone UTF-16 surrogates deterministic before UTF-8 and the output alphabet contains no dot. The canonical pair key is `cook.v1.<userComponent>.<recipeComponent>`. Tests prove delimiter/control/dot/colon/surrogate/Unicode pairs cannot alias and decode round-trips exact UTF-16 code units. Raw concatenation is forbidden.
- The Worker derives the canonical DO address as `env.COOK_SESSIONS.idFromName(canonicalPairKey(userId, recipeId))`. The exported SQLite class is exactly `CookSessionDurableObject`; the `Env` binding is exactly `COOK_SESSIONS: DurableObjectNamespace<CookSessionDurableObject>` in production and QA. `wrangler.json` has top-level and `env.qa` `durable_objects.bindings` entries `{ "name": "COOK_SESSIONS", "class_name": "CookSessionDurableObject" }`; migration tag is exactly `v1_cook_sessions` with `new_sqlite_classes: ["CookSessionDurableObject"]`. That deterministic per-user/per-recipe object, not D1, arbitrates start/resume and guarantees one active attempt. Parallel starts serialize in the same object.
- Every new attempt gets a random `attemptId` UUID stored inside the DO and returned in snapshots. D1 stores one history/index row per attempt and retains nullable unique `activeKey = canonicalPairKey(userId, recipeId)` as a projection integrity check, but start/resume never consults D1 to decide canonical state.
- Active recipes are cookable by any authenticated user because the current product has public active recipes. One per-instance promise-tail FIFO gate wraps every DO `fetch()` lifecycle/residue/upgrade handler, `alarm()`, and state-reading `webSocketMessage()` through all awaits; completion or rejection always releases the tail, while `webSocketClose()`/`webSocketError()` perform only their synchronous handshake matrix outside it. Cloudflare's single active object instance plus persisted state covers restarts; the gate is not persisted and carries no canonical state. After corruption, expiry, replay, and current-state precedence inside that gate proves a new attempt is needed, the DO itself executes one D1 `batch()` transaction containing the visibility Recipe SELECT plus all RecipeStep/Ingredient/Unit/IngredientRef/step-output-use SELECTs required for the snapshot; no Worker prefetch or independent Prisma reads are allowed. D1 batch completion is only the pinned-snapshot read point. The later single DO storage transaction atomically writing history/coordinator/current/start-ledger/projection/alarm is the accepted-attempt linearization point; failure/crash before that commit accepts nothing, and retry rereads D1. Parallel starts wait on the gate, then losers observe and resume the winner. A delete/edit committed before the batch is observed; one committed after may yield a pre-change pinned attempt even when its commit precedes the later DO storage commit. Missing, soft-deleted, or future visibility-inaccessible recipes return indistinguishable `404 not_found`; terminal/current coordinator state remains. Both race orders plus deferred-D1 parallel starts, alarm/message interleaving, gate rejection release, and D1-success/DO-commit-failure are tested. No recipe-ownership restriction is introduced. Once created, the pinned attempt remains owner-accessible without re-reading Recipe visibility, and active start/resume returns it after later edit/soft-delete. Uncoordinated hard deletion is outside this guarantee. The recipe route falls back to the authenticated caller's own current pinned snapshot when public lookup fails; callers without their own attempt receive ordinary 404.
- `GET /api/cook-sessions/recipes/:recipeId` returns `200 { snapshot }` from the authenticated user's deterministic DO. `PATCH` accepts exact `{ attemptId, baseRevision, mutationId, operations }`, with one to 64 operations from exactly: `{ type: "set_active_step", stepIndex }`, `{ type: "set_scale_factor", scaleFactor }`, `{ type: "set_ingredient_checked", ingredientId, checked }`, and `{ type: "set_step_output_checked", stepOutputId, checked }`. `POST /api/cook-sessions/recipes/:recipeId/complete` and `/abandon` each accept exact `{ attemptId, baseRevision, mutationId }`. Every terminal/PATCH body rejects missing/extra keys and wrong types as `422 validation_error` after valid JSON parsing and before DO state; mutationId/attemptId are lowercase UUID-v4 and baseRevision is a nonnegative safe integer. `ingredientId` is exactly `CookRecipeSnapshot.Ingredient.id`, never ingredientRefId; `stepOutputId` is exactly StepOutputUse.id, never outputStepId. Accepted/live-replayed mutations return `200` with the current evolved snapshot; request hashing excludes mutationId exactly as defined next.
- Every `requestHash` is lowercase hexadecimal SHA-256 of UTF-8 recursively sorted-key canonical JSON. Hash objects are exact: start `{ type: "start", recipeId, adoption? }` with omission preserved and present checked arrays lexicographically sorted; PATCH `{ type: "patch", attemptId, baseRevision, operations }`; complete `{ type: "complete", attemptId, baseRevision }`; abandon `{ type: "abandon", attemptId, baseRevision }`. Mutation/request ids are excluded; PATCH operation array order is preserved. Pinned traversal order is used for applied state, never start hashing. PATCH structural validation before DO state lookup covers exact keys/types, one-to-64 count, safe integers/booleans, and finite generic scale bounds; pinned step-index bounds and ingredient/output membership are semantic validation. After persisted-head and replay/attempt/PURGING/terminal precedence, semantic validation runs against the current pinned snapshot before revision/capacity. Operations execute sequentially; duplicate targets are allowed and last wins, then checked arrays are re-emitted in pinned traversal order. A structurally invalid request changes nothing; a semantically invalid request may persist only expiry pruning.
- Revision-zero defaults are `activeStepIndex: 0`, `scaleFactor: 1`, empty checked arrays, ACTIVE status, null terminal timestamps, and one clock reading used for equal `startedAt`/`updatedAt`. Cook revisions are `0..2_147_483_646`; projection sequence may use `2_147_483_647` for the final purge DELETE. Each accepted non-replayed PATCH increments revision exactly once regardless of operation count or no-op values; `updatedAt` becomes `max(clockNow, previousUpdatedAt + 1ms)`. First complete/abandon increments once, computes the same monotonic updatedAt, sets its selected completedAt/abandonedAt exactly equal to that updatedAt, returns `200 { snapshot }`, and enqueues terminal projection. An increment when revision is already `2_147_483_646`, or when `previousUpdatedAt+1` exceeds JavaScript's `8_640_000_000_000_000` Date limit, changes nothing and returns `409 numeric_limit`. Opposite terminal target returns `409 terminal_conflict`; same-target fresh id records a no-op response without revision/time change when capacity remains. A valid purge is the sole status transition that preserves both revision and updatedAt: it changes only status to PURGING and preserves prior terminal timestamps. Completion never creates a RecipeSpoon/notification.
- Start and progress/terminal records use one safe integer-millisecond clock: `acceptedAtMs`, `expiresAtMs = acceptedAtMs + 86_400_000`, live iff `nowMs < expiresAtMs`; equality is expired. Platform clock values must be nonnegative safe integers at most `8_639_999_913_600_000`; invalid platform time is `500 internal_error` before writes. After structural/corrupt-head validation, every state-changing DO request captures one nowMs and prunes expired records before state precedence. Global start capacity 64 counts live starts plus start tombstones. Mutation capacity 256 is attempt-scoped and counts that attempt's live records plus tombstones; older-attempt tombstones never consume a newer attempt's count. `Retry-After = max(1, ceil((oldestRelevantExpiresAtMs-nowMs)/1000))`. No unexpired guarantee is evicted. Only accepted mutations create live records. Live records contain request hash/status/outcome/revision metadata, never recipe/progress snapshots; while a non-PURGING attempt remains current, exact replay returns the recorded HTTP status/outcome plus the current evolved snapshot. Reuse with another hash returns mutation_conflict. Replacement/purge converts records to non-content tombstones. Tombstone count is at most `64 + (64 * 256) = 16,448`, and the byte-reservation rule below may apply backpressure sooner; none may be evicted before expiry. Tombstones are excluded from live-session-state residue counts but remain identifier-bearing retained metadata and are reported as such. Stale revision includes latest snapshot; network uncertainty retries canonical-equivalent original id first.
- A fresh start mutation while current is `COMPLETED` or `ABANDONED` atomically creates a new ACTIVE attempt at revision zero and returns `201` with `server_won` for supplied adoption or `not_requested` when absent. One storage transaction persists new current/coordinator/start record and create projection, converts every unexpired start record and every unexpired mutation record targeting the terminal attempt to `attempt_replaced` tombstones, and deletes the now-empty old mutation ledger; only afterward are old sockets closed `4000 Attempt replaced`. Before transaction commit every request observes the complete old terminal state/replays; after commit every old-id replay observes 410; crash/exception exposes no intermediate mix. A start while current is ACTIVE resumes it with 200.
- `GET /api/cook-sessions/recipes/:recipeId/live` requires a same-origin WebSocket upgrade. Server frames are exactly `{ type: "snapshot", snapshot }` and `{ type: "error", error: { code, message }, snapshot? }`. The server sends an initial snapshot and broadcasts after accepted progress or terminal transitions. PURGING uses repeated best-effort, duplicate-tolerant send attempts because `WebSocket.send()` returns no delivery acknowledgement and cannot be made crash-atomic with socket state: every purge fence/alarm/event/wake attempt calls `send(current PURGING snapshot)` and then `close(4001,"Session purged")` in program order; a crash or close failure may produce duplicate byte-equivalent PURGING snapshots, which clients accept idempotently. Neither at-least-once delivery nor exactly-once delivery is claimed. An upgrade validated after the fence calls send with `session_purging` plus PURGING snapshot then closes 4001. Replacement/wake sends `stale_attempt` plus latest then closes 4000; missing sends `not_found` then closes `4000 Attempt unavailable`; state-load failure sends `internal_error` then closes `1011 Internal error`. Client data closes `1003 Read-only subscription`; normal client close is 1000. Attachments remain exact `{ version: 1, userId, recipeId, attemptId }`; no fictitious delivery flag is persisted.
- A live-route GET that passes auth/origin but lacks exact case-insensitive `Upgrade: websocket` returns `426 upgrade_required` / `WebSocket upgrade required.`, `Upgrade: websocket`, and ordinary private JSON headers; an upgrade with missing/invalid Cloudflare `webSocket` pair fails ordinary 500 before 101. `webSocketMessage()` enters the FIFO gate, validates attachment/state/queue, and applies PURGING -> stale -> missing precedence before otherwise closing 1003 for any client payload. `webSocketClose(webSocket,code,reason,wasClean)` always attempts synchronous `webSocket.close(code,reason)` to complete the close handshake, swallowing only that close exception and changing no storage/alarm. `webSocketError(webSocket)` attempts `close(1011,"WebSocket error")`, swallows a close exception, and changes no storage/alarm. Tests call all handlers directly under the repository compatibility date.
- Upgrade attachment failure returns ordinary `500 internal_error` before 101. After 101, a synchronous initial-snapshot `send()` exception attempts close `1011 Initial snapshot failed`; close failure is swallowed and the socket is left for later event validation. For every error frame, attempt the specified close code/reason even if `send()` throws; synchronous send/close errors never change DO state or an already-selected HTTP/upgrade outcome. Replacement attempts stale frame then 4000 for every old socket independently; failures do not roll back the new attempt and a survivor is revalidated on its next event/wake. Accepted non-purge progress/terminal state and projection enqueue commit before fanout; healthy sockets continue, a thrown send attempts `1011 Broadcast failed`, failed close is swallowed, HTTP remains 200, and no broadcast retry alarm is scheduled. Purge persists fence/barrier/alarm first, then for every socket attempts PURGING snapshot and 4001 independently regardless of send exception; failures never roll back or change DELETE 202. While PURGING, every alarm/event/wake retries 4001 on every attached socket. A send/close exception or any socket still returned by `ctx.getWebSockets()` advances only the independent persisted socket retry channel; projection success/failure never clears or delays it. Purge cannot commit its coordinator tombstone or return 204 until `ctx.getWebSockets()` is empty; silent sockets therefore keep DELETE at 202 and remain visible in residue rather than being forgotten. Clients recover by reconnect initial snapshot/GET.
- `DELETE /api/cook-sessions/recipes/:recipeId` accepts `{ attemptId }` and is not mutation-ledger-backed. While current exists only matching id may purge; another id is stale_attempt. With no current, unexpired lastPurged match is bodyless 204 and another id 404. Matching purge, including repeats while pending, returns exact `202` data `{ snapshot, purgeStatus: "pending" }`; snapshot is PURGING. After coordinator tombstone commit it returns bodyless 204. Valid purge atomically changes only status to PURGING while preserving revision/updatedAt/terminal timestamps, appends its reserved barrier, broadcasts, and closes sockets. For any structurally valid start/snapshot/PATCH/complete/abandon request while current is PURGING, `409 session_purging` with current `{ snapshot }` takes precedence over exact live replay, hash conflict, tombstone, attempt id, terminal, revision, semantic, and capacity checks. Thus a formerly accepted id temporarily returns purging, then returns `410 attempt_purged` after purge commit; upgrades use the frame matrix. DELETE retains its special matching/stale behavior above. The alarm drains older projections, deletes current D1 row, and closes sockets. Only after zero sockets does it remove all five live-state keys and convert live replays.
- Coordinator stores no recipe/progress content, sets `coordinatorExpiresAtMs = purgeAcceptedAtMs + 86_400_000`, and shares the single DO alarm at the minimum of projection retry, socket retry, and metadata deadline. At `nowMs >= coordinatorExpiresAtMs`, coordinator and expired tombstones are logically invalid immediately: replay/DELETE behaves as absent even if bytes remain. An alarm at/after that deadline physically deletes coordinator/tombstones when no current/five keys/sockets remain; failure throws for Cloudflare retry and each later alarm reevaluates cleanup. Physical deletion has eventual, not exact-24-hour, timing. A fresh attempt clears coordinator expiry but permanent content-free `history:v1` remains and forces server_won adoption. Release proof requires zero relational product rows and zero content-bearing/live-state DO data, while separately attesting that permanent history plus identifier-bearing coordinator/tombstones remain under the exact logical-expiry contract; it never calls that metadata erased or product-data zero.
- Failure behavior is fixed: local persistence failure before the PURGING fence leaves state unchanged and returns `500`; broadcast/socket-close failure after persistence never rolls back the fence but retains PURGING and an alarm until no attached socket remains; older-projection D1 failure retains queue/barrier/content; current-row D1 delete failure retains barrier/content; a crash after D1 delete retries that delete idempotently; failed atomic live-state-key deletion/tombstone write retains content/barrier and retries; success is reported only after the tombstone is committed, all five live-state keys are absent, and `ctx.getWebSockets()` is empty.
- `GET /api/cook-sessions/recipes/:recipeId/residue` is an existing-user owner-authenticated, same-origin, non-OpenAPI diagnostic used before disposable-user deletion. It returns the standard JSON success envelope whose `data` is exact `{ historyEverStarted, currentAttemptId, lastPurgedAttemptId, presentKeys, projectionHeadValid, liveStateKeyCount, pendingProjectionCount, liveSocketCount, coordinatorExpiresAtMs, tombstoneCount, tombstoneMaxExpiresAtMs }`. `presentKeys` is a lexicographically sorted subset of the eight exact keys below; expiry fields are safe integer/null; counts are nonnegative safe integers. `liveStateKeyCount` counts presence of the five current/start/mutation/queue/retry keys even if a value is corrupt. `pendingProjectionCount` is zero when the queue key is absent or its value is not an exact object with an own array `entries`; otherwise it is that raw array length. The retained wire name `projectionHeadValid` is true only when the queue is absent or its wrapper, every entry, and all queue-wide identity/order invariants validate, so a corrupt tail cannot be hidden behind a healthy head. It never returns hashes, mutation ids, recipe/progress content, or tombstone bodies, but `lastPurgedAttemptId` and tombstone count/expiry explicitly attest that retained identifier-bearing metadata exists. A malformed queue still returns 200 with `projectionHeadValid:false` plus the deterministic count/key evidence; every other lifecycle/read/upgrade and `alarm()` returns 500/throws before changing or projecting anything. Cleanup captures this exact allowlist before disposable-user deletion. After deletion all cook routes verify the User row, return 401, clear the stale cookie, and cannot access the DO; no post-delete owner call is required or permitted.
- Request precedence is exact. First resolve route/method (404/405), then validate signed session and require its User row exists in D1; missing row returns `401 authentication_required` with expired session cookie before Origin/body/DO. D1 auth lookup failure is 500. State-changing requests, `/residue`, and every `/live` request then run one shared server-side same-origin guard before body parse, DO namespace lookup, WebSocket allocation, or 426/101 selection; snapshot GET alone is exempt. The guard requires one byte-exact `Origin === new URL(request.url).origin`, rejecting absent, `null`, comma-joined/duplicate, malformed, or mismatched values. When `Sec-Fetch-Site` is present it must be byte-exact `same-origin`; every other value is rejected. Any guard failure returns ordinary private `403 invalid_origin` and creates no mutation/subscription. Parse/structurally validate before DO. Every lifecycle read/write/upgrade validates every present storage string, its canonical encoding/byte bound, and the complete projection queue before state or replay; malformed/oversized wrapper/head/tail gives ordinary 500 before 101 and changes nothing. `/residue` alone reports queue corruption diagnostically as above. Next prune state-changing expiry. If current PURGING, all non-DELETE lifecycle routes return session_purging before replay/tombstone/attempt. Otherwise lookup replay/tombstone, require attempt, apply terminal rules, semantic validation, revision/numeric checks, non-queue candidate/response/frame size (413), relevant ledger count plus eventual-tombstone byte reserve (429), then projection count/byte reserve (503), in that order. A new start performs its D1 batch at the declared point, then applies recipe/current/response size, start-ledger/tombstone reserve, and projection reserve before the acceptance transaction. Unexpected storage errors map 500.
- State-changing HTTP requests, `/residue`, and `/live` enforce the shared same-origin guard above; endpoints use cookie sessions and are excluded from v1/OpenAPI. Exact mapping adds to the existing table: `409 numeric_limit` / `Cook session numeric limit reached; start fresh.`, `413 cook_session_too_large` / `Recipe is too large for synchronized cook progress.`, `426 upgrade_required` / `WebSocket upgrade required.`, `503 projection_backlog` / `Cook session projection backlog is full; retry later.`, and retains `400 invalid_json` / `Request body must be valid JSON.`, `401 authentication_required` / `Authentication required.`, `403 invalid_origin` / `Origin must match request origin.`, `404 not_found` / `Cook session or recipe not found.`, `405 method_not_allowed` / `Method not allowed.`, `409 stale_attempt` / `The cook attempt is no longer current.`, `409 stale_revision` / `Cook session revision is stale.`, `409 mutation_conflict` / `mutationId was already used for a different request.`, `409 terminal_conflict` / `Cook session already has a different terminal status.`, `409 session_terminal` / `Cook session is terminal.`, `409 session_purging` / `Cook session purge is in progress.`, `410 attempt_replaced` / `The recorded cook attempt was replaced.`, `410 attempt_purged` / `The recorded cook attempt was purged.`, `422 validation_error` / `Request body is invalid.`, `429 start_ledger_full` / `Cook session start ledger is full; retry after records expire.`, `429 mutation_ledger_full` / `Cook session mutation ledger is full; retry after records expire.`, `500 internal_error` / `Internal server error.` Session_purging includes current snapshot. Projection backlog carries `Retry-After: 60`; both ledger-full errors use the oldest relevant expiry rule. Size errors are permanent contract 4xx on the client and require recipe simplification rather than automatic retry.
- Exact `Allow` values/order are: start base `POST`; recipe base `GET, PATCH, DELETE`; `/live` `GET`; `/complete` `POST`; `/abandon` `POST`; `/residue` `GET`. HEAD is not promoted to GET. Unknown paths return 404 without Allow.
- Browser transport is exact. Every fetch sets `credentials:"same-origin"`, `cache:"no-store"`, `Accept:"application/json"`, and a fresh physical-request `X-Request-Id: req_<lowercase UUID-v4>`; GET has no Content-Type/body, while POST/PATCH/DELETE set `Content-Type:"application/json"` and `JSON.stringify` the exact body. Browser-managed Origin/Cookie headers are never manually set. A network retry reuses mutationId/body but gets a new request id. Live URL is `new URL('/api/cook-sessions/recipes/'+encodeURIComponent(recipeId)+'/live', window.location.href)` with protocol mapped `https:` to `wss:` and `http:` to `ws:`, same host/port/query-empty/hash-empty, `new WebSocket(url)` with no subprotocol; ambient same-origin cookies authenticate it.

**Cook Snapshot, Offline, And Projection**
- `CookRecipeSnapshot` is exactly `{ version: 1, id: string, title: string, coverImageUrl: string|null, steps: Step[] }`. Each step is `{ id: string, stepNum: safe integer, stepTitle: string|null, description: string, duration: safe integer|null, ingredients: Ingredient[], stepOutputUses: StepOutputUse[] }`. Each ingredient is `{ id: string, ingredientRefId: string, name: string, quantity: finite number, unit: { id: string, name: string } }`. Each step-output use is `{ id: string, outputStepId: string, outputStepNum: safe integer, outputStepTitle: string|null }`. Stable ids must be nonempty; stored strings including empty are preserved. Zero/negative step/output/duration values are legal; unsafe integers are invalid snapshot source data. activeStepIndex addresses sorted-array position.
- Snapshot construction sorts steps by `(stepNum, id)`, ingredients within a step by `id`, and step-output uses by `(outputStepNum, id)`. Canonicalization recursively sorts object keys lexicographically; preserves array order, stored Unicode code points, case, and whitespace; includes every schema field and emits nullable values as JSON `null`; never emits `undefined`; rejects non-finite numbers; normalizes `-0` to `0`; and otherwise uses ECMAScript JSON number serialization. The fingerprint is lowercase hexadecimal SHA-256 of the UTF-8 canonical recipe-snapshot JSON. Database timestamps and other non-schema fields are excluded.
- `CookSessionSnapshot` is exactly `{ version: 1, attemptId: lowercase UUID-v4, recipeId: string, recipeFingerprint: 64-char lowercase hex, recipe: CookRecipeSnapshot, revision: nonnegative safe integer, status, activeStepIndex: safe integer, scaleFactor: finite number, checkedIngredientIds: string[], checkedStepOutputIds: string[], startedAt: canonical ISO string, updatedAt: canonical ISO string, completedAt: canonical ISO string|null, abandonedAt: canonical ISO string|null }`. UUID-v4 everywhere matches `^[0-9a-f]{8}-[0-9a-f]{4}-4[0-9a-f]{3}-[89ab][0-9a-f]{3}-[0-9a-f]{12}$` without normalization. Every wire/storage integer uses `Number.isSafeInteger` plus its declared range. Status is ACTIVE/COMPLETED/ABANDONED/PURGING; active index is zero for empty else in bounds; scale 0.25..50. Checked ingredient IDs are duplicate-free subsets of Ingredient.id emitted in step-then-ingredient pinned traversal order; checked output IDs are StepOutputUse.id emitted in step-then-use pinned traversal order. Every server/client/anonymous snapshot write uses that order. ACTIVE has null terminals; terminal timestamp equals its monotonic updatedAt; PURGING preserves prior revision/updatedAt/terminal shape. Pristine adoption applies pinned order; server-won is never applied.
- The SQLite-backed DO permits exactly eight keys and no extra fields. Every present value is stored as one canonical JSON UTF-8 string and parsed/validated on read. `history:v1` is permanent `{ version:1, everStarted:true }`. `coordinator:v1` is `{ version:1,userId,recipeId,currentAttemptId:UUID|null,lastPurgedAttemptId:UUID|null,coordinatorExpiresAtMs:safe-integer|null }`. `current-attempt:v1` is `{ version:1,userId,recipeId,snapshot }`. `start-ledger:v1` is `{ version:1,entries:StartEntry[] }`; StartEntry is `{ mutationId,requestHash,attemptId,statusCode:200|201,adoptionOutcome,acceptedRevision,acceptedAtMs,expiresAtMs }`. `mutation-ledger:v1` is `{ version:1,attemptId,entries:MutationEntry[] }`; MutationEntry is `{ mutationId,requestHash,attemptId,statusCode:200,acceptedRevision,acceptedAtMs,expiresAtMs }`. `projection-queue:v1` is `{ version:1,entries:ProjectionEntry[] }`. `retry-state:v1` is `{ version:1,projection:RetryChannel|null,sockets:RetryChannel|null }`, where each `RetryChannel` is exact `{ failures:integer 1..5,nextAlarmAtMs:nonnegative safe integer at most 8_640_000_000_000_000 }`; projection is nonnull only with a nonempty valid queue, sockets is nonnull only with a PURGING current attempt, a null channel means no pending retry for that concern, both null deletes the key, stored five saturates as defined in the alarm transition, and every alarm-time addition is range-checked before persistence. `replay-tombstones:v1` is `{ version:1,entries:Tombstone[] }`; Tombstone is `{ ledger:"start"|"mutation",mutationId,requestHash,attemptId,outcome:"attempt_replaced"|"attempt_purged",expiresAtMs }`.
- Serialized-byte limits are exact and measured with `TextEncoder` over the exact canonical JSON string before any write/send. The pinned `CookRecipeSnapshot` may use at most 262,144 bytes. Every persisted key value may use at most 1,500,000 bytes, and every HTTP success/error or WebSocket frame containing a snapshot may use at most 1,000,000 bytes. A start whose built recipe/candidate current/response exceeds its limit, or a PATCH/terminal candidate whose non-queue state or response/frame exceeds its limit, returns `413 cook_session_too_large` with no storage, ledger, revision, projection, alarm, or socket change. Each such acceptance also preflights the exact synthetic same-snapshot PURGING variant for current storage, response, and socket error/snapshot frames, so a later purge can never be blocked by one added status byte. Reads validate stored byte limits before schema/state; an oversized stored value is corruption and fails closed. Before accepting any start/mutation, compute the eventual tombstone wrapper using every existing tombstone plus every unexpired live record and the candidate represented with worst-size outcome `attempt_replaced`; if that wrapper would exceed 1,500,000 bytes, apply the relevant start/mutation ledger-full backpressure before writes, so later replacement/purge conversion to either outcome can never overflow. Fixed count caps still apply.
- Ordering/identity is exact. Start/mutation entries sort `(acceptedAtMs,mutationId)` numeric/BINARY; tombstones sort `(expiresAtMs,ledger,mutationId)` numeric/BINARY; queue preserves FIFO append order. The DO name components equal coordinator/current userId+recipeId; coordinator currentAttemptId null iff no current key; a current snapshot's recipe/attempt equals coordinator/current wrapper; mutation-ledger wrapper and all entries equal current attempt; each live entry's attempt matches its wrapper/current attempt, and `acceptedRevision` is the exact revision produced by that acceptance but is audit metadata only. Tombstones carry no snapshot/revision. History must exist whenever coordinator/current/live ledgers/tombstones ever existed. Unknown/misordered/duplicate entries, cross-key mismatch, oversized value, invalid canonical JSON, or extra field is corruption. Empty start/mutation/queue/retry/tombstone keys are deleted. Five live-state keys remain current/start/mutation/queue/retry; history is content-free permanent arbitration metadata, coordinator/tombstones are bounded identifier-bearing idempotency metadata, and WebSockets are runtime-only.
- Active cooking renders the pinned snapshot. When the current recipe fingerprint differs, the UI offers `Continue original` or `Start fresh`; start-fresh abandons the old attempt before creating a new one.
- Root-owned `CookSessionDeviceProvider` lives above `Outlet` for every authenticated route. It gives each top-level browsing context a UUID-v4 `clientId` in sessionStorage key `spoonjoy-auth-cook-client:v1`; reload/session restore retains it. Before any authenticated record access, the provider holds exclusive Web Lock `spoonjoy-auth-cook-client:<clientId>` for the provider lifetime across route navigation, trying a retained id immediately then after 50/100/200 ms before a cloned tab generates a new id. Every record mutation additionally acquires shared Web Lock `spoonjoy-auth-cook-user:<userComponent>`; reset/logout/identity cleanup acquires that same lock exclusively. Lock ordering is lifetime client lock then user lock, never the reverse, and no code waits on another user lock while holding one. Missing Web Locks support or acquisition/storage failure blocks cook state with exact `Cook progress can't open safely in this browser.` Authenticated record prefix is `spoonjoy-auth-cook:v1.<userComponent>.<recipeComponent>.` and the exact key appends `<clientId>`; reset key is `spoonjoy-auth-cook-reset:v1.<userComponent>.<recipeComponent>`. Persistent generation keys are `spoonjoy-auth-cook-user-generation:v1.<userComponent>` and `spoonjoy-auth-cook-recipe-generation:v1.<userComponent>.<recipeComponent>`. Components come only from `storageIdComponent`, and prefix deletion never uses raw ids.
- Each generation value is exact `{ version:1,userId,generation:nonnegative-safe-integer }` for user scope and `{ version:1,userId,recipeId,generation:nonnegative-safe-integer }` for recipe scope. Missing generation initializes to zero under the relevant user lock; cleanup advances its target generation by exactly one before deleting records, and safe-integer exhaustion blocks cleanup without deletion. The record's exact value is `{ version: 1, userId, recipeId, clientId, userGeneration, recipeGeneration, attemptId: UUID-v4|null, snapshot: CookSessionSnapshot|null, pending: CookOperation[], inFlight: InFlight|null, command: Command|null }`, serialized as recursively lexicographically sorted-key canonical JSON with array order preserved and written by one `setItem`. Immediately before every ordinary record `setItem`/`removeItem`, while holding the shared user lock, re-read and validate the global marker, matching scoped marker, and both generation keys; any applicable marker, malformed/read-failed value, or generation mismatch blocks the write and network send. Exclusive cleanup deletion is the sole exception: it requires its own exact valid marker/target generation and never reacquires a shared lock. `CookOperation` is the exact PATCH operation union. `InFlight` is `{ type: "patch", mutationId: UUID-v4, attemptId: UUID-v4, baseRevision: nonnegative integer, operations: CookOperation[1..64] }`. `Command` is Start `{ type: "start", mutationId, recipeId, adoption: AdoptionInput|null }`, Terminal `{ type: "complete"|"abandon", mutationId, attemptId, baseRevision }`, or StartFresh `{ type: "start_fresh", phase: "abandon"|"start", abandon: { mutationId, attemptId, baseRevision }, start: { mutationId, recipeId, adoption: null } }`. Pending has 0..256 operations in queue order and no duplicate target after coalescing. `attemptId` and `snapshot` are both null or both match; pending/inFlight require an ACTIVE matching snapshot; inFlight attempt matches the record; command and inFlight are mutually exclusive; every command requires empty pending/inFlight because start/start-fresh begin empty and terminals wait for drain. Tabs converge only through the DO/WebSocket.
- Session/local storage read errors, invalid lowercase UUID clientId, unknown record/generation version/field, malformed snapshot/operation/command, or broken invariant preserve offending bytes, keep bootstrap closed, render `Cook progress on this device is corrupted.`, and send nothing. Confirmed reset acquires the exclusive user lock and writes exact marker `{ version:1,userId,recipeId,startedAtMs,fromGeneration,toGeneration }`, where both generations are safe integers and `toGeneration===fromGeneration+1`. In that lock, current recipe generation must equal fromGeneration (write exact toGeneration) or toGeneration (resume after crash); any other value is corruption. It then deletes only the exact encoded record prefix in lexicographic key order, rescans to zero, removes the marker, and releases. Failure before marker write removes nothing; every later partial failure retains the same marker and target generation with `Retry device cleanup`, so resume never increments twice. Marker creation/storage events make every matching tab close socket, clear memory, remove its sessionStorage client-id key, and block sends. Generation mismatch fences a delayed storage event or late writer even after marker removal; the affected tab must rebootstrap with the new generation before writing. No server/other-user/other-recipe state is removed. A new operation coalesces same target; operation 257 rejects without write/eviction and renders exact `This device already has 256 pending cook changes. Reconnect or retry before adding more.`
- Logout/user switch uses persistent localStorage marker `spoonjoy-auth-cook-cleanup:v1` = `{ version:1,departingUserId,startedAtMs,fromGeneration,toGeneration }` with the same exact +1/current-equals-from-or-to resume rule. Root `CookSessionDeviceProvider` owns identity-change observation and exposes `CookSessionLogoutForm`; both existing logout forms use it. App-initiated logout acquires the departing user's exclusive lock, writes/reuses the marker, writes exact toGeneration once, closes/clears departing contexts, deletes encoded departing prefixes in lexicographic order, and rescans to zero before submitting the existing `/logout` POST while still holding both marker and lock. A status/redirect alone is not confirmation: the root provider must observe its revalidated loader identity become null or a different user after that response. Only then does it remove the marker and release; action/network failure or unchanged/unknown loader identity retains the marker for explicit retry and no incoming bootstrap begins. On resume, a still-authenticated departing identity retries the POST, while a loader-confirmed absent/different identity follows the already-departed branch without reposting. For server 401/external cookie loss, the identity is already confirmed departed, so the same exclusive cleanup may remove the marker after zero rescan. A user switch keeps the departing fence through confirmed identity transition, then bootstraps the incoming user only after release. An existing marker is processed before current identity bootstrap; a different requested transition waits. Incoming/unrelated prefixes and generation keys are never removed.
- Marker parsing is fail-closed. Invalid JSON, unknown version/extra field, unsafe time, empty/mismatched ids, wrong key/value scope, or malformed generation renders exact `Cook progress cleanup marker is corrupted.`, blocks all affected reset tabs (and all cook tabs for the global logout marker), preserves bytes, and performs no deletion/network. A corrupt scoped reset marker may be overwritten with a freshly valid same-scope marker only after explicit `Reset device cleanup`; a corrupt global marker has unknown scope and can only be removed by explicit `Clear corrupted cook cleanup marker`, which deletes no record, broadcasts the removal, then restarts identity bootstrap. A valid logout marker for another departing user is not corruption: finish it first; a requested conflicting transition waits. Tests force a writer to pause before shared-lock acquisition, complete reset/logout under the exclusive lock, delay every storage event, then prove the writer cannot restore deleted bytes because its generations are stale; they also prove an already-held shared write finishes before cleanup deletion and cannot land afterward.
- Coalesce pending-only same targets by remove-old/append-new. Pending max 256; batch max 64. Persist every inFlight/command before send; failure sends nothing. Ordinary accepted start/complete/abandon persists snapshot then clears its command. Start Fresh preallocates both UUIDs and persists the full phase-abandon chain before sending abandon. Accepted/replayed abandon, a terminal_conflict followed by GET proving that same attempt is terminal in either terminal status, or any other GET proving that same attempt terminal atomically persists its terminal snapshot plus the same chain at phase start before sending start; StartFresh intent wins and is never handled by the ordinary terminal-conflict clear rule. A stale/different attempt discards the chain and adopts canonical state. Accepted start persists the new snapshot then clears the chain. Phase-start 404 persists a cleared chain/idle error `Recipe is no longer available to start.`; conflict/retry follows ordinary start with fresh id persisted inside chain. While command exists controls are disabled. No authenticated mutation sends from memory only.
- If persisting any accepted PATCH/start/terminal response fails, render canonical server state; PATCH reapplies pending only. Reject actions/sends and retain replay-safe disk. For StartFresh abandon response failure, render terminal while disk remains phase abandon; same-mount Retry-saving writes terminal+phase-start locally without re-sending abandon and may then send persisted start, while reload replays exact abandon before advancing. For StartFresh start response failure, same-mount Retry-saving writes/clears locally without network; reload replays exact start. Local persistence retries only by visible Retry saving or one per focus, never a timer. Sync unblocks after persistence. Anonymous progress clears only after start response plus authenticated record persistence.
- Every authenticated mount has a canonical bootstrap barrier. Parse this tab's record but render/send nothing. Replay ordinary command first; StartFresh replays its persisted phase. Otherwise GET canonical state, persist same-attempt base then resolve inFlight, replace different attempt with empty queues, write the exact idle record on 404, and run persistent departing-user cleanup on 401. Persistence failure keeps barrier closed. Reload recovers every StartFresh boundary; simultaneous tabs use stale-revision rebase. A destroyed context's client-scoped record is intentionally not auto-recovered, sent, or garbage-collected because another context cannot safely merge its queue; it remains inert until same-recipe Reset device cleanup or departing-user cleanup deletes the encoded prefix. While pending/inFlight/command exists or accepted memory is not yet persisted, render exact `Keep this tab open until cook progress finishes syncing.` and install `beforeunload` with `preventDefault()` plus `returnValue=""`; remove both only when that predicate clears. Offline reload never trusts disk.
- Pending/inFlight transition and display are exact. With no command/inFlight, sending atomically moves the first at-most-64 pending operations into a new persisted InFlight (same order), removes them from pending, then sends; persistence failure sends nothing. Display is always `apply(base snapshot, inFlight.operations if any, then pending in queue order)`, so the move causes no visual change. Network/unknown response retains byte-identical inFlight. An unsolicited GET/WebSocket higher base is persisted under the inFlight and both overlays remain; the original mutation id is retried to resolve accepted-versus-stale. A direct accepted/replayed PATCH response persists its snapshot and clears inFlight before applying pending. Stale revision replaces base, replaces inFlight mutationId/baseRevision with a fresh persisted id/revision while preserving its operations, then retries. Different attempt clears both overlays. If accepted-response persistence fails, memory renders the accepted canonical snapshot plus pending only (known-accepted inFlight is not overlaid), disk remains unchanged, sends block, and visible Retry-saving persists canonical/cleared inFlight before resuming.
- Every accepted HTTP/WebSocket snapshot passes the persistence gate. Higher same-attempt revision replaces base under the exact overlays above; lower/equal-identical is ignored. Same-attempt non-PURGING to byte-equivalent-fields PURGING is the sole legal equal-revision/different-content transition and persists directly. Every other equal-different source allows exactly one canonical confirmation GET per attempt/revision; a confirming equal-different blocks with exact `Cook progress could not be synchronized because the server returned conflicting state.` until explicit Retry.
- Anonymous storage remains `spoonjoy-cook-progress:<recipeId>`. Valid v2 is exact `{ version: 2, recipeFingerprint, activeStepIndex, scaleFactor, checkedIngredientIds, checkedStepOutputIds, updatedAt }` with exact keys, lowercase fingerprint, safe index, finite bounded scale, canonical ISO updatedAt, duplicate-free in-bounds arrays in traversal order. Only current-fingerprint valid v2 adopts. Malformed JSON/v2, same-fingerprint invalid v2, and mismatched v2 are never filtered/adopted: render empty current-fingerprint state in memory, preserve raw bytes until first local action, then overwrite with valid current-fingerprint v2 containing that action. Existing v1 alone keeps legacy filtering/local-only behavior and remains v1. Anonymous clears only after authenticated start response plus authenticated persistence.
- Error disposition is exact. Stale revision rebases as above; PATCH mutation conflict GETs and retries only same ACTIVE attempt; start conflict GETs then persists/retries unchanged start/adoption with fresh id; ordinary terminal conflict retries only same ACTIVE, otherwise clears its ordinary command/adopts fetched; StartFresh uses its phase rule. Stale/replaced clears overlays then GETs. Purged/not-found atomically writes the exact idle record `{...identity,attemptId:null,snapshot:null,pending:[],inFlight:null,command:null}`; remove/write failure keeps old disk and blocks. Purging persists supplied PURGING or GETs once. A 401 first completes the persistent departing-user cleanup protocol, then clears auth; marker failure blocks. Network/408/425/429/5xx retain byte-equivalent inFlight/command and retry only on bootstrap/online/reconnect/Retry, honoring valid Retry-After. Contract 4xx/unknown retains and blocks. Adoption never trusts client time.
- Live subscription starts only after bootstrap has persisted an ACTIVE canonical snapshot. A mount owns at most one CONNECTING/OPEN socket and one reconnect GET through a generation token; replacing/unmounting or a successfully persisted terminal snapshot closes the old socket with 1000 and never reconnects. Stale callbacks do nothing. A WebSocket `error` starts a 5-second close-event watchdog; close cancels it, while expiry invalidates/closes that generation and enters abnormal-close recovery. Close 1000 stops; 1003 is a protocol error requiring explicit Retry; 4000 immediately GETs canonical state before any new socket. On 4001, a successfully persisted preceding PURGING snapshot selects the blocked PURGING state; without such a persisted frame, perform exactly one canonical GET before choosing PURGING, terminal, or 404-idle, and apply ordinary retry classes if that GET fails. No 4001 path reconnects a socket until explicit fresh start. Codes 1001/1006/1011 and other abnormal closes, watchdog expiry, or upgrade failure observed as 1006 schedule fixed 1/2/4/8/16/30-second GET-before-reconnect attempts, then 30 seconds indefinitely. Offline cancels the timer; `online` and explicit Retry trigger immediate GET. GET 401 clears auth, 404 becomes idle, 429 waits Retry-After, network/408/425/5xx use backoff, and contract 4xx/protocol failures block for explicit Retry. Backoff resets only after open plus initial snapshot successfully persists. Snapshot persistence failure closes with 1000, performs local Retry-saving only, then reconnects after persistence succeeds. Queue/network retry runs only after reconnect GET/snapshot persistence; no duplicate socket or concurrent reconnect GET is allowed.
- The DO is canonical; D1 has owner-private metadata. My Kitchen queries at most 12 ACTIVE cards ordered updatedAt/attemptId descending. Continue activation has one request/timer: ACTIVE navigates exact hash; terminal/404 hides and permanently invalidates card for the mount; session_purging consumes required snapshot, GET-rearms the alarm, hides card, and shows one `Finishing cleanup...` row. Purging/transient network/408/425/5xx auto-GET at 1/2/4/8/16/30 seconds then every 30 seconds while visible+online; 429 uses valid Retry-After else the same next backoff. Focus/online triggers immediate GET and cancels duplicate timer. 401 runs auth cleanup; malformed response or other contract 4xx keeps card with explicit error/Retry and no timer. Any ACTIVE result resets backoff; terminal/404 removes status; unmount stops. Loader revalidation cannot re-add an invalidated id in that mount. Authenticated recipe detail including pinned fallback, `/saved-recipes`, My Recipes, and owner My Kitchen sets private no-store/Pragma/deduplicated Vary Cookie; anonymous behavior remains.
- The lifecycle smoke creates one disposable active recipe with exactly two steps, at least one Ingredient.id, and one StepOutputUse.id, then exactly attempts A/B. A start is accepted 201 but its response body/id is discarded; residue and canonical GET rediscover A at revision 0. Two independent browser contexts GET A, open sockets, and record initial rev0. Client 1 PATCHes activeStepIndex 1 -> rev1; both observe rev1. Client 2 checks the ingredient -> rev2; both observe. Client 1 in one ordered PATCH checks the output and sets scale 2 -> rev3; both observe exact pinned arrays/scale. The recipe is edited after pinning; both reload detail, capture mismatch warning, choose Continue original, and retain A/rev3. Client 2 completes at base3 -> rev4 and both observe terminal. Fresh start creates B rev0; both GET it. Client 2 sets scale 1.5 -> rev1, both observe; Client 1 abandons base1 -> rev2 and both observe. Cleanup purges B; A's content-free DO history remains, while its terminal D1 projection is removed only by the cleanup-only user-scoped projection retirement after A's hashed retirement proof and before user deletion. Each HTTP timeout is 10s, each frame poll is 100ms/max15s, and each D1 projection poll is 1s/max60s. Functional setup-through-B-abandon has its own hard 120-second deadline and never cancels finally cleanup. Cleanup then has independent primary 90 seconds, optional exact 5-second handoff, and recovery 90 seconds, for a maximum 185 cleanup seconds and 305 seconds after functional start. Artifacts include sanitized ordered exchanges, socket frames/context, diagnostics, the mismatch screenshot, residue snapshots, D1 rows, and cleanup trace. Test-only malformed decoder affects A's discarded response and never creates C.
- Every lifecycle/visual request, response, frame, error, report, and owning command stdout/stderr passes one shared fail-closed sanitizer before any filesystem write, console output, or hash; raw transport bytes remain memory-only and are never hashed. `SanitizedLocation={route,queryCategories}` uses finite `route:'auth_login'|'auth_signup'|'home'|'cook_base'|'cook_recipe'|'cook_live'|'cook_complete'|'cook_abandon'|'cook_residue'|'recipe_detail'|'recipe_edit'|'recipes_index'|'user_kitchen'|'saved_recipes'|'my_recipes'|'health'|'unknown'` and sorted unique `queryCategories:('cursor'|'filter'|'mutation'|'other')[]`; URL parsing discards scheme, userinfo, host, port, every dynamic path segment, every query value, fragment, and raw unknown route/query text before classification. Header objects are no-extra-fields subsets of `cache-control|content-type|pragma|retry-after|x-spoonjoy-build-sha|x-spoonjoy-worker-version`: cache-control is exactly `private, no-store|no-store|no-cache`, content-type exactly `application/json|application/json; charset=utf-8|text/html; charset=utf-8`, pragma exactly `no-cache`, Retry-After canonical decimal `1..300`, build SHA exactly the command's expected Sha, and Worker version exactly the expected UUID when supplied. Raw request id is compared in memory and discarded; it is never a header value in artifacts. Any noncanonical retained value, unexpected key, expected-SHA/version mismatch, or duplicate header aborts sanitization before write/log/hash and removes partial output.
- `CookSnapshotEvidence={kind:'snapshot',recipeId,attemptId,recipeFingerprint,revision,status,activeStepIndex,scaleFactor,checkedIngredientIds,checkedStepOutputIds,startedAt,updatedAt,completedAt,abandonedAt}` is no-extra-fields; identifiers/fingerprint, integer/range, duplicate-free checked arrays in pinned step/ingredient and step/output-use traversal order, status/timestamp/nullability, and scale use the live snapshot contract. `CookPurgeEvidence={kind:'purge',snapshot,purgeStatus:'pending'}` requires snapshot PURGING. `CookResidueEvidence={kind:'residue',historyEverStarted,currentAttemptId,lastPurgedAttemptId,presentKeys,projectionHeadValid,liveStateKeyCount,pendingProjectionCount,liveSocketCount,coordinatorExpiresAtMs,tombstoneCount,tombstoneMaxExpiresAtMs}` exactly projects the diagnostic contract. `CookWireErrorCode` is the exact finite union `invalid_json|authentication_required|invalid_origin|not_found|method_not_allowed|numeric_limit|cook_session_too_large|projection_backlog|stale_attempt|stale_revision|mutation_conflict|terminal_conflict|session_terminal|session_purging|attempt_replaced|attempt_purged|validation_error|start_ledger_full|mutation_ledger_full|upgrade_required|internal_error`. `CookErrorEvidence={kind:'error',code,status,currentAttemptId,currentRevision}` is no-extra-fields; code is CookWireErrorCode and status must equal its exact wire mapping from the lifecycle table, including `upgrade_required -> 426`. currentAttemptId is lowercase UUID-v4/null and currentRevision is nonnegative safe integer/null; both are nonnull exactly for `stale_attempt|stale_revision|session_purging`, equal the required raw `data.snapshot.attemptId/revision`, and are both null for every other code whose raw error forbids data. `CookWireFrameErrorCode` is the exact four-member server union `stale_attempt|session_purging|not_found|internal_error`; only these codes may appear in raw server error frames or SanitizedFrame. Local protocol failure and unrecognized input use SanitizedDiagnostic code `protocol` or `unknown` and can never become a SanitizedFrame, CookErrorEvidence, or passed release evidence. `SanitizedCookValue` is exactly the four-member snapshot/purge/residue/error union. `SanitizedBody` is exactly `{kind:'empty'}`, `{kind:'cook-json',value:SanitizedCookValue}` for a classified cook response only, or `{kind:'redacted',categories}` with sorted unique finite `categories:('credential'|'profile'|'session'|'token'|'mutation'|'unknown')[]`; every request body is redacted, and no raw field name/value/length/digest/prefix is stored. In lifecycle/visual transport-derived non-image structured/text artifacts, recipe/profile/ingredient/output text, raw or redirect/query/userinfo URLs, free-form error data, response messages, and unknown string-bearing fields are absent. Schema-declared canonical provider/PR/check/workflow/job/base/health URLs in release evidence are the explicit allowlist and are not lifecycle transport projection. Before projection, recursively reject normalized sensitive keys `password|passcode|secret|token|accesstoken|refreshtoken|idtoken|apikey|clientsecret|codeverifier|credential|session`. Disposable email remains memory-only; persisted identity uses emailSha256.
- `SanitizedExchange={sequence,at,method,location,status,requestIdMatched,requestHeaders,responseHeaders,requestBody,responseBody}` and `SanitizedDiagnostic={sequence,at,level,code,method,location,status}` are no-extra-fields. Methods are `GET|POST|PUT|PATCH|DELETE`; exchange status is safe integer `100..599`; requestIdMatched is boolean and must be true for a passed HTTP exchange. Diagnostic level is `info|error`, code is `request|response|protocol|timeout|cleanup|browser|assertion|sanitizer|review|unknown`, and method/location/status are nullable exact values. `SanitizedFrame` is exactly `{kind:'snapshot',sequence,at,context,snapshot:CookSnapshotEvidence}` or `{kind:'error',sequence,at,context,code,snapshot}` with context `client1|client2`, code CookWireFrameErrorCode, and snapshot CookSnapshotEvidence/null. Error-frame snapshot is nonnull and byte-equals the raw frame snapshot exactly for `stale_attempt|session_purging`; it is null for `not_found|internal_error`. Within each exchange, frame, or diagnostic stream sequence is contiguous from 1 and canonical ISO times are nondecreasing; cross-referenced at values are equal byte-for-byte. Any local parse/protocol/unrecognized error maps to SanitizedDiagnostic code `protocol|unknown` without raw name/code/message/stack/cause and cannot produce a frame or pass release. Lifecycle/visual stdout and stderr are NDJSON diagnostics only. WebSocket artifacts contain only validated server SanitizedFrame values, never upgrade headers, raw frame bytes, or local diagnostic pseudo-frames. Screenshots are the sole binary exception: before each capture, the runner proves auth forms/password inputs absent, scans rendered text plus value/title/aria-label/alt/href/action attributes for its in-memory email/password/token/URL sentinels, and refuses the image if any match; only fixed disposable fixture content may remain visible. Tests inject unique secret sentinels into URL user/password/path/query keys/values/fragments, every rejected header name/value including UUID-shaped request ids, nested/body-key names, schema-valid recipe text/URLs, auth responses, email, exception name/code/message/cause/stack, cleanup failures, frames, rendered DOM attributes, and stdout/stderr; every noncanonical union/status/sequence/time/header or sentinel match fails before hashes are accepted and removes partial output.
- Raw projection ownership begins in Unit29.2, before any smoke runtime. Pure import-safe `scripts/release-artifact-contract.mjs` exports the sole `projectCookHttpBody(transportStatus,rawBodyInput)` and `projectCookFrame(rawFrame,context,sequence,at)` functions plus exact schema parsers; it has no filesystem, process, network, clock, smoke, visual-runner, or release-evidence import. `RawCookHttpBody` is the exact no-extra-fields input union `{kind:'empty'}` or `{kind:'json',value:unknown}`. The runtime adapter reads response bytes in memory: exact byteLength zero becomes empty; otherwise fatal UTF-8 decoding plus JSON.parse must succeed and becomes json, so literal `null`, whitespace, malformed UTF-8/JSON, and zero bytes remain distinguishable. transportStatus is mandatory and must be a JavaScript safe integer in exact HTTP range `100..599`; missing/undefined/null, booleans, strings, objects, fractional values, NaN, either infinity, unsafe integers, values below 100, and values above 599 reject before body inspection. The HTTP projector's success matrix is exact: start envelope `{ok:true,requestId,data:{snapshot,adoptionOutcome}}` accepts only 200/201 and validates adoptionOutcome; ordinary snapshot envelope `{ok:true,requestId,data:{snapshot}}` accepts only 200; purge envelope accepts only 202; residue envelope accepts only 200; and only `{kind:'empty'}` accepts 204. Every cross-kind/status pairing, empty under non-204, and json under 204 rejects. For every raw error it requires transportStatus, `error.status`, and the lifecycle table's CookWireErrorCode mapping to agree and writes that same value into CookErrorEvidence.status. It validates no-extra-fields envelopes, required `data.snapshot` versus forbidden data, and current identity/revision equality before returning SanitizedBody; start projects its validated snapshot while discarding adoptionOutcome. A mismatch throws before output. Callers construct SanitizedExchange.status from the same immutable validated transportStatus, and artifact ingestion rejects any exchange/body status disagreement. `projectCookFrame` accepts only a valid snapshot frame or one of the exact four CookWireFrameErrorCode values with required/forbidden snapshot equality; it rejects `protocol_error`, `unknown`, and every unrecognized raw code. Invalid raw input throws before returning bytes. `release-evidence.ts` imports/re-exports these projectors for Unit29.2's self-contained raw fixtures and uses the parsers for artifact ingestion; Unit30's `smoke-live-helpers.mjs` imports the same module for runtime projection. Unit29.2 exhaustively owns the RawCookHttpBody union and every transportStatus boundary, including valid 100/599 reaching ordinary envelope/status rejection; source/import-graph tests reject another projector or any dependency from this module to Unit30/31 runtime files.
- `smoke-results.json.lifecycleEvents` is one authoritative no-extra-fields transition ledger, separate from per-client observation frames. `LifecycleStartEvent={kind:'start',sequence,at,recipeId,attemptId,revision:0,status:'ACTIVE',source}` uses source `residue|response`; `LifecycleProgressEvent={kind:'progress',sequence,at,recipeId,attemptId,revision,status:'ACTIVE',activeStepIndex,scaleFactor,checkedIngredientIds,checkedStepOutputIds}` uses the snapshot bounds; `LifecycleTerminalEvent={kind:'terminal',sequence,at,recipeId,attemptId,revision,status}` uses status `COMPLETED|ABANDONED`; `LifecycleResidueEvent={kind:'residue',sequence,at,recipeId,residue:CookResidueEvidence}` requires the final live-zero allowlist. The ledger is exactly this union, has contiguous sequence from 1 and strictly increasing canonical at values, and contains one server-accepted event per transition: A start0/progress1/2/3/terminal4, later B start0/progress1/terminal2, then one final residue for their recipe. Each event hash is SHA-256 over UTF-8 `JSON.stringify` of the no-extra-fields object inserted in the declared field order, with no replacer or whitespace. `FinalResidue={recipeId,eventSequence,eventSha256,residue}` is no-extra-fields, cross-links the unique residue event byte/hash, and is sorted by recipeId; phase finalResidues contains exactly one per distinct report recipe. RetiredAttempt.terminalSnapshotSha256 equals the unique A terminal-event hash, replacementStartSha256 equals the unique later B start-event hash, and finalResidueSha256 equals FinalResidue.eventSha256. A release report rejects duplicate/missing/out-of-order transitions, a second matching terminal/start/residue, any identity/revision/status/time mismatch, or a hash over any other bytes.
- `scripts/production-visual-dogfood.mjs` is the import-safe task-owned Playwright runner behind exact package command `production:visual-dogfood`; it imports, rather than duplicates, the shared sanitizer and cleanup-proof writer from `scripts/smoke-live-helpers.mjs`. It requires explicit `--base-url`, `--source-sha`, `--worker-version-id`, and fresh `--out`, verifies exact health before auth, creates exactly one disposable authenticated user plus anonymous contexts, writes only the closed sanitized visual set, and completes its own primary cleanup proof before success. Focused tests exercise every runner branch and sentinel path; script typecheck and full-suite 100% coverage include it before Unit32 freezes HEAD. Unit37 invokes this exact ProcessCommand under logical name `production-visual-dogfood`, then uses the execution-contract-defined `production-visual-qa-review:visual_qa` and `production-visual-design-review:design_visual` AgentCommand prompts against the live site and immutable artifacts; a finding that needs no code may retry Unit37, while a code finding must enter the post-merge successor-task protocol and can never mutate this already-merged branch or edit artifacts in place.
- Visual artifact content is exact and no-extra-fields. `VisualCaptureId` is the ordered 29-member set `guest-home-mobile|guest-home-desktop|guest-home-wide|cook-session-mobile|cook-session-desktop|continue-cooking-mobile|continue-cooking-desktop|saved-controls-mobile|saved-controls-desktop|saved-kitchen-mobile|saved-kitchen-desktop|saved-recipes-mobile|saved-recipes-desktop|tag-authoring-mobile|tag-authoring-desktop|tag-discovery-mobile|tag-discovery-desktop|tag-display-detail-mobile|tag-display-detail-desktop|tag-display-list-mobile|tag-display-list-desktop|tag-display-card-mobile|tag-display-card-desktop|developer-docs-mobile|developer-docs-desktop|api-playground-mobile|api-playground-desktop|mcp-guide-mobile|mcp-guide-desktop`. One immutable registry derives basename `<viewport>-<surface>.png` from each id and maps surfaces to the actual changed route exactly: guest-home/continue-cooking/saved-kitchen -> `home`; cook-session -> `cook_recipe`; saved-controls/tag-display-detail -> `recipe_detail`; saved-recipes -> `saved_recipes`; tag-authoring -> `recipe_edit`; tag-discovery -> `my_recipes`; tag-display-list -> `recipes_index`; tag-display-card -> `user_kitchen`; developer-docs -> `developer_docs` at canonical `/api`; api-playground -> `api_playground` at canonical `/api/playground`; mcp-guide -> `mcp` at `/mcp`. Redirect aliases are tested but do not duplicate screenshots. Mobile is 390x844, desktop 1440x900, wide 1920x1080. Guest-home and mcp-guide use fixture `guest`; developer-docs uses public `guest`; api-playground uses `authenticated` with one saved recipe containing source URL, nonsequential steps, scalable quantity, course, and custom tags.
