Saved-recipes mobile uses `saved-populated-search` and must show multiple saved results plus the active search/filter state; saved-recipes desktop uses `saved-empty-search` and must show the authenticated no-match state; every other non-display id except tag-display uses `authenticated`; tag-display mobile uses `dense` and desktop uses `empty`. `VisualCapture={id,route,viewport,fixture,screenshot,screenshotSha256,status:'passed',authFormCount:0,passwordInputCount:0,sensitiveTextMatchCount:0}` must match that registry exactly. `VisualReport={version:1,sourceSha,workerVersionId,captures,cleanupOutcomePath:'cleanup-outcome.json'}` uses exact expected source/Worker values and the ordered 29 captures. `VisualMetric={captureId,screenshotSha256,viewportWidth,viewportHeight,scrollWidth,horizontalOverflowPx,overlapCount,occludedControlCount,clippedTextCount,nextSectionVisible}` matches the capture registry; screenshotSha256 must equal that id's VisualCapture hash and decoded PNG bytes, dimensions/scrollWidth/horizontalOverflowPx/counts are nonnegative safe integers, horizontalOverflowPx is `max(0,scrollWidth-viewportWidth)` and at most 1, all three counts are zero, and nextSectionVisible is true exactly for guest-home captures and null otherwise. `VisualMetrics={version:1,metrics}` contains the exact capture order and therefore binds every metric to the validated PNG hash. `absurdity-ledger.md` is exact UTF-8 bytes `# Visual Absurdity Ledger\nversion: 1\nstatus: closed\nready: 0\nreviewer_gated: 0\nfindings: none\n`; no free-form prose is accepted.
- Every screenshot must decode as one PNG with exact registry dimensions, one IHDR/IEND, no bytes after IEND, and no `tEXt`, `zTXt`, `iTXt`, or `eXIf` chunk; malformed dimensions/chunks/CRC/trailing data reject the artifact before hash acceptance. Unit29.2's literal fixtures use tiny deterministic valid registry-dimension PNG builders and corruption cases without importing or executing the later visual runner.
- After the runner atomically closes its exact 38-file tree, form one entry per direct child file with `path` equal to that output-relative basename only (no slash, prefix, task-relative, or absolute form) and sha256 equal to its bytes; sort entries by path using UTF-8/BINARY order. `visualArtifactSetSha256` is SHA-256 over UTF-8 `JSON.stringify` of that exact ordered `{path,sha256}` list with declared field order and no replacer/whitespace. Each visual reviewer runs against that immutable set; reviewer output is accepted only as exact CONVERGED or the canonical sanitized FINDINGS JSON. A FINDINGS verdict writes and hashes `review-findings.v1.json`, then fails its command/stage. On CONVERGED, the executor writes one canonical UTF-8 report with exact eight newline-terminated lines `# Spoonjoy Production Visual Review`, `version: 1`, `role: <visual_qa|design_visual>`, `agent_id: <canonical lowercase UUID>`, `verdict: clean`, `source_sha: <mergeSha>`, `visual_artifact_set_sha256: <sha256>`, `open_findings: 0`. Any extra line/field, invalid agent id, different source/set hash, non-clean verdict, or nonzero finding rejects the report before hashing. This format applies respectively to `visual-qa-review.md` and `visual-design-review.md` and stores no finding text.
- Each primary or recovery cleanup pass has `deadline=started+90_000`, 30 total I/O attempts, nested 20 cook HTTP attempts. Before any attempt fail when `now >= deadline`, total count already 30, or cook count already 20; then increment applicable counters and use timeout `min(10_000,deadline-now)`. Logical operationAttempt starts 1 and increments on retry, resetting only when phase/target changes. Network, 408/425/5xx, and 429 retry; Retry-After is valid only `/^[1-9][0-9]*$/` integer seconds, otherwise absent; delay is valid Retry-After else `min(500*2^(operationAttempt-1),5000)`. Fail before sleep when `now+delay >= deadline`. D1/admin failures retry only the same statuses or exact case-insensitive tokens `rate limit`, `timed out`, `ETIMEDOUT`, `ECONNRESET`, `fetch failed`; malformed/unmatched/nonzero is fatal. Primary/recovery budgets reset independently.
- Cleanup state machine is exact. GET residue 200 must parse the standard envelope and exact diagnostic `data` schema; malformed envelope/data, corruption, or other 4xx is fatal, while retry classes above retry. Cleanup targets only its predeclared purgeTarget. Residue current matching that target issues DELETE; DELETE 202 or either GET/DELETE 409 `session_purging` waits exactly 1000ms, increments operationAttempt without resetting phase/target, and then spends the next bounded I/O attempt on canonical residue GET. The same deadline/attempt guards run before that sleep and GET; no other polling interval is legal. 409 stale_attempt with any other current id and every 404 are fatal identity/proof failures. Residue current null with matching unexpired lastPurged still issues one idempotent confirmation DELETE, which must return bodyless 204; any required-target path passes only after this exact terminal 204, then one final residue. Residue current null with live-state/projection/socket data, missing/mismatched lastPurged, or any DELETE for a non-target is fatal. Final proof requires presentKeys subset exactly `history:v1`, `coordinator:v1`, `replay-tombstones:v1`; history true; current/five live-state keys/sockets zero; coordinator current null with logical expiry; tombstone max expiry at/before coordinator expiry. Capture this retained-DO proof and exact A retirement, require no nonterminal/activeKey D1 row, then use the existing scoped Wrangler D1 command runner to execute one parameterized userId plus retired-attempt-id DELETE against CookSessionIndex only. The command may delete exactly the retired A row and never B/another user/table; it runs under the same bounded D1/admin retry budget, atomically returns changes plus remaining user rows, and is followed by a zero-row query. Record the immutable projection-retirement receipt inside pre-delete proof, then delete user. Visual has no retired attempt, skips mutation, and records the zero/empty receipt. After deletion make no owner DO call; prove User and all CookSessionIndex rows zero and rely on mandatory User-existence auth to make retained metadata inaccessible. Release claims distinguish relational/content-bearing/live-state zero from permanent content-free history plus bounded/logically expiring identifier-bearing idempotency metadata.
- Cleanup runs in finally. Primary failure records phase/evidence, waits exactly 5 seconds only if `now+5000 < deadline` (otherwise starts recovery immediately), then one recovery with fresh budgets. Recovery checks user existence first. Absent user makes zero owner calls, reuses immutable pre-delete DO proof and the prepared user-delete mutation journal, writes the truthful reconciled user-delete proof only when the original response was lost, then rechecks user absence plus all-D1-zero and post-delete evidence. Present user repeats the state machine, including projection-response reconciliation. Exact flags remain: clean functional+primary exits zero; functional failure with clean primary exits nonzero/residueClean true; recovered cleanup exits nonzero/residueClean+cleanupRecovered true; two failures residueClean false/cleanupIncomplete true.

**CookSessionIndex Projection Schema**
- D1 model `CookSessionIndex` has: `attemptId String @id`, `userId String`, `recipeId String`, nullable unique `activeKey String?`, `status String`, `recipeFingerprint String`, `recipeTitle String`, `recipeCoverImageUrl String?`, `activeStepIndex Int`, `scaleFactor Float`, `checkedIngredientCount Int`, `checkedStepOutputCount Int`, `revision Int`, `projectionSeq Int`, `lastProjectionId String @unique`, `startedAt DateTime`, `updatedAt DateTime`, `completedAt DateTime?`, and `abandonedAt DateTime?`; user/recipe foreign keys cascade on hard delete. Indexes are `(userId,status,updatedAt)`, `(userId,recipeId,startedAt)`, and `(recipeId)` plus the unique active key/projection id constraints. It stores no full recipe/progress/checklist content.
- Persisted queue entries are a discriminated union. UPSERT is `{ version: 1, projectionId: "<attemptId>:<sequence>:UPSERT", attemptId, sequence, kind: "UPSERT", payload }`, where payload is exactly `{ userId, recipeId, status: "ACTIVE"|"COMPLETED"|"ABANDONED", recipeFingerprint, recipeTitle, recipeCoverImageUrl: string|null, activeStepIndex, scaleFactor, checkedIngredientCount, checkedStepOutputCount, revision, startedAt, updatedAt, completedAt: string|null, abandonedAt: string|null }`. DELETE is `{ version: 1, projectionId: "<attemptId>:<sequence>:DELETE", attemptId, sequence, kind: "DELETE", payload: { userId, recipeId } }`; PURGING is never UPSERTed. Sequence/revision/count/index fields are nonnegative integers (scale finite in range), fingerprints/ids/status/timestamp nullability match the snapshot, and every timestamp is canonical `Date.toISOString()` text. Initial create sequence/revision is 0; progress/terminal UPSERT uses resulting revision; purge DELETE uses current revision + 1. Every enqueue, dequeue, lifecycle load, and alarm validates the exact wrapper plus every entry's version, fields, projectionId components, immutable owner/recipe/attempt, sequence/payload revision equality for UPSERT, timestamp/status shape, and FIFO cross-entry invariants. Any malformed persisted wrapper/head/tail remains byte-for-byte queued and has the exact fail-closed precedence above; `alarm()` throws and nothing is dropped or sent to D1. Against an existing D1 row, matching `lastProjectionId` is an exact no-op; greater sequence applies; lower sequence is a no-op; equal sequence with a different projectionId is projection corruption, throws, and never overwrites/deletes. A missing-row UPSERT applies; a missing-row DELETE replay is a no-op. A greater DELETE removes the row; lower is a no-op; equal-different is corruption. Applied UPSERT sets activeKey only for ACTIVE and records lastProjectionId. FIFO orders old terminal, new active, and purge across attempts.
- Queue-wide invariants are exact: length is `0..1_024`; projectionId is unique; every payload userId/recipeId equals the deterministic object's owner/recipe; each attempt occupies at most one contiguous block; and within each block entries retain append order with strictly increasing sequence, at most one DELETE, DELETE last, and no UPSERT after DELETE. The first still-queued sequence need not be zero because successful heads are deleted. Old-attempt blocks precede later-attempt blocks, including old terminal before new create; validation never re-sorts.
- Projection queue capacity is both 1,024 entries and 1,500,000 canonical UTF-8 bytes, with the final slot and enough bytes for one exact current-attempt DELETE reserved exclusively for purge. Before any ordinary append, serialize the candidate queue plus a synthetic DELETE using the current owner/recipe/attempt and maximum legal sequence `2_147_483_647`; acceptance requires current length `< 1,023` and that reserved wrapper remain within the byte limit. Otherwise return `503 projection_backlog`, `Retry-After: 60`, and record no state/ledger/revision. ACTIVE resume/same-terminal no-op/exact replay append nothing and remain available. A previously accepted queue therefore guarantees purge can append at length at most 1,023, yielding at most 1,024; an existing purge DELETE is reused, and no other transition can append while PURGING. A structurally valid but already oversized queue is corruption/500 rather than capacity. Successful alarm dequeue reopens count/byte capacity; no entry is evicted or coalesced.
- Every start/progress/terminal/purge transition that appends a projection calls top-level SQLite DO storage writes plus `setAlarm(Date.now())` inside the same explicit `ctx.storage.transaction`; no external I/O occurs inside. Alarm and state/ledger/revision/queue commit atomically. `setAlarm` failure aborts everything, records no mutation id, and returns `500 internal_error`, so client retry is fresh. The first alarm is immediate. One FIFO-gated alarm invocation validates all persisted state, then independently runs every due channel: it processes at most 32 projection heads sequentially and, while current is PURGING, performs one complete socket sweep when the socket channel is due. For each projection head it performs exactly one idempotent D1 transaction, then one DO transaction verifies/removes that exact unchanged head and clears only `retry-state.projection`; it may continue through head 32. A socket sweep attempts PURGING send then close for every attached socket independently; zero remaining sockets clears only `retry-state.sockets`, while any thrown operation or remaining socket advances only that channel. Projection and socket work due in the same alarm are both attempted even when the other fails. After both channels, PURGING finalization runs only when its DELETE barrier is gone and the socket set is empty. The next alarm is immediate when a projection queue remains after 32, otherwise the minimum of both retry channels and coordinator/tombstone metadata deadlines; no remaining work deletes the alarm. D1 success followed by DO-commit failure leaves the head and relies on D1 replay no-op under Cloudflare alarm retry.
- Projection and socket channels use independent consecutive-failure transitions. First through fifth failures for that channel persist `failures=1..5` and delays 2/4/8/16/32 seconds; when its stored failures is already five, every later failure keeps five and delays 60 seconds indefinitely. A successful projection head clears only projection retry before a later head can establish a fresh sequence; a successful socket sweep that reaches zero clears only socket retry. Initial purge fanout that leaves/throws on any socket establishes socket failure one even if projection work also fails. Each head-removal transaction is already durable before the next head; the final retry-state/alarm transaction is computed from the post-work queue/socket state and atomically updates both channels plus the one minimum alarm. If that final transaction fails, prior successful head removals and their per-head projection-channel clears remain valid; the thrown alarm retries from the newly persisted queue and last committed retry state without inventing either channel. Card GET rearming is repair only, never the sole creation path. Unit13 tests all due/not-due cross-products, independent counter/reset behavior, minimum-alarm precedence, socket-only PURGING retries, and finalization after both barriers clear.

**SavedRecipe**
- `SavedRecipe(userId, recipeId, createdAt)` uses composite primary key `(userId, recipeId)`, required foreign keys to User and Recipe with `ON DELETE CASCADE`, `createdAt NOT NULL DEFAULT CURRENT_TIMESTAMP`, and index `(userId, createdAt, recipeId)`. Explicit unsave hard-deletes only this row.
- Migration `0026_saved_recipes.sql` backfills each active `(Cookbook.authorId, RecipeInCookbook.recipeId)` once with `createdAt = MIN(RecipeInCookbook.createdAt)` across that author's matching cookbook memberships, using an explicit `JOIN Recipe ON Recipe.id = RecipeInCookbook.recipeId WHERE Recipe.deletedAt IS NULL`, conflict-ignore semantics, and no replacement/deletion. `addedById` does not determine ownership. Rerunning is harmless and preserves the first saved timestamp.
- Adding cookbook membership through `recipe-detail.server.ts`, `cookbooks.$id.tsx`, `spoonjoy-api.server.ts`, or `api-v1.server.ts` uses one shared D1-safe helper that submits membership create/upsert and SavedRecipe upsert together through Prisma's non-interactive `$transaction([promise, promise])` batch form; callback/interactive transactions are forbidden for this helper. Removing membership never unsaves; explicit unsave never removes cookbook membership. Re-save is idempotent. Soft-deleted recipes remain referenced but are hidden until restored.
- `/saved-recipes` and owner-only My Kitchen sections use SavedRecipe. My Kitchen shows at most 12 active saves ordered `(SavedRecipe.createdAt DESC, recipeId DESC)` plus a link to `/saved-recipes`; the dedicated route remains complete. Saved search is a viewer-scoped SQL path: join/EXISTS SavedRecipe before ordering, never post-filter an already-limited global result. A blank query returns every active saved recipe ordered `(SavedRecipe.createdAt DESC, recipeId DESC)`. A nonblank query applies the existing recipe FTS parser, intersects before ordering, returns every match ordered by existing BM25 rank, then title `COLLATE NOCASE`, then recipeId; the web route introduces no limit or pagination. Tests exceed the global 50-result maximum to prove completeness. Private save state is never written to global `SearchDocument` metadata or duplicate documents.
- Web save uses the existing `POST /recipes/:id` FormData action with exact intent `saveRecipe` or `unsaveRecipe`; recipe id comes only from the route. Before dispatch, inspect all entries: if any `intent` entry is either save value, the body is valid only when it contains that one string entry and nothing else; mixed-order `intent=other&intent=saveRecipe`, repeated save values, an extra key, a File, or blank returns bodyless `400`. When no save value appears, existing non-save intents retain current field handling, but a missing, blank, or otherwise unknown first intent returns bodyless `400` after authentication. It requires cookie auth through existing `requireUserId(request, "/login", env)`, so an unauthenticated POST throws `302 Location: /login?redirectTo=/recipes/<id>` before parsing the body. Success is JSON `200 { ok: true, intent, recipeId, saved }` with `Cache-Control: private, no-store`, `Pragma: no-cache`, and `Vary: Cookie`; it calls idempotent save/unsave without a client mutation id. Missing/soft-deleted recipe is bodyless `404`; already desired state is 200. The fetcher disables only this control while pending, does not optimistically flip, updates only when the response intent and recipeId match its submitted command, and on a route error, network failure, malformed/mismatched 200 body, or non-200 preserves prior state with inline `Couldn't update saved recipes.` plus Retry of the same idempotent intent. Cookbook controls are unaffected.
- Public v1 adds exact private authenticated routes `GET /api/v1/me/saved-recipes` requiring `kitchen:read` and `PUT|DELETE /api/v1/me/saved-recipes/{recipeId}` requiring `kitchen:write`. Existing cookie-session and bearer principals are accepted through the existing v1 principal resolver; absent/insufficient principals use existing errors, and every response uses private no-store. GET accepts at most one limit/cursor; repeated, blank cursor, or blank/invalid limit is validation error. Limit defaults 20/max50 and order is createdAt DESC, recipeId DESC. Cursor is unpadded `v1.<base64url>` using `[A-Za-z0-9_-]+`; decoded UTF-8 must be byte-exact `JSON.stringify({ createdAt, recipeId })` with only those keys/order, canonical Date.toISOString round-trip, nonempty recipeId, and raw re-encoding equality. Padding, invalid UTF-8/alphabet, noncanonical JSON/ISO, or extra/missing/type-invalid keys is invalid. Predicate is strict `createdAt < cursor.createdAt OR (createdAt = cursor.createdAt AND recipeId < cursor.recipeId)` independent of cursor-row existence. Query requests limit+1; return first limit, hasMore iff extra row, and nextCursor from last returned row only when hasMore, else null. Response cursor echoes accepted raw or null. Recipes are active viewer saves with isSaved true.
- PUT and DELETE on that exact mutation path use existing v1 idempotency and accept `clientMutationId` from JSON body, then `X-Client-Mutation-Id`, then query string, in that precedence order; unknown body fields are rejected. Both return `200` with `{ recipeId, saved: true|false, mutation: { clientMutationId, replayed: false } }`; existing idempotency replay changes only `replayed` to true while retaining the recorded status/body. PUT of an already-saved recipe and DELETE of an already-unsaved active recipe are successful. Missing or soft-deleted recipes return `404`; unsave never changes cookbook membership.
- Personalized REST recipe `isSaved` is a separate optional projection privilege, never an implication of public recipe access. Cookie-session and trusted environment principals receive their user's boolean. A bearer principal receives a boolean only when its normalized granted scopes contain exact `kitchen:read`; `public:read`, `recipes:read`, `kitchen:write` without `kitchen:read`, and every other read-capable scope receive null and perform no SavedRecipe lookup. Invalid tokens and principals lacking the endpoint's ordinary recipe-read scope retain existing errors. Every valid authenticated request, including a public-only bearer whose value is null, is `private, no-store` with Pragma and deduplicated `Vary: Cookie, Authorization`; only a request with no principal uses the existing public Cache-Control/ETag behavior.

**RecipeTag**
- `RecipeTag` is exact: `id TEXT PRIMARY KEY NOT NULL` / Prisma `String @id @default(cuid())`; required `recipeId`, `label`, `normalizedLabel`, `kind`, `source`, `createdById`; and required `createdAt`/`updatedAt` defaulting to `CURRENT_TIMESTAMP` (`updatedAt @updatedAt` in Prisma). `recipeId` references Recipe with `ON DELETE CASCADE`; `createdById` references User with `ON DELETE CASCADE`. SQL CHECKs constrain kind to `COURSE|CUSTOM` and source to `MANUAL`. Unique `(recipeId, normalizedLabel)` enforces normalized identity in addition to the partial one-COURSE index. Supporting indexes are `(recipeId, kind, normalizedLabel, id)`, `(kind, normalizedLabel, recipeId)`, and `(createdById)`. Hard-deleting either parent removes tags; soft-deleting a recipe preserves but hides them.
- `kind` is `COURSE` or `CUSTOM`; `source` is `MANUAL` in this release. Only the recipe owner may mutate tags. Manual tags are canonical immediately and have no acceptance transition.
- Course is optional/singular with values main/side/appetizer/dessert; a CUSTOM normalizedLabel equal to one of those four is reserved and invalid. Before normalization reject any unpaired UTF-16 high/low surrogate; never replacement-normalize it. Custom display canonicalization uses exactly whitespace U+0009..000D, U+0020, U+0085, U+00A0, U+1680, U+2000..200A, U+2028, U+2029, U+202F, U+205F, U+3000; U+FEFF is preserved. Strip leading/trailing members, collapse each interior maximal run to ASCII space, preserve all else/casing, enforce 1..40 Unicode scalar values, then `display.normalize("NFKC").toLowerCase()`. Scalar comparator iterates well-formed code points, compares numeric values, then shorter sequence, never localeCompare; SQL uses BINARY. Tests include unpaired `\uD800`/`\uDC00` rejection, `A< U+FEFF < B` preservation, composed/decomposed NFKC identity, supplementary U+1F600 ordering after BMP U+FFFF, and prefix-before-longer ordering.
- Database invariants are exact. Partial unique index permits one COURSE. BEFORE INSERT and BEFORE UPDATE OF `kind,normalizedLabel,recipeId` triggers raise literal `recipe_tag_custom_limit` only when NEW is a distinct CUSTOM and the target recipe already has ten other CUSTOM rows (UPDATE excludes OLD.id); duplicate conflict-ignore never trips the limit. AFTER INSERT/DELETE and actual UPDATE of label/normalizedLabel/kind/source set parent Recipe.updatedAt to SQL `CURRENT_TIMESTAMP`; same-second equality is legal because RecipeTag contentHash, not parent time alone, drives search freshness. Validation maps course cardinality/value to `Choose one valid course.`, malformed/length custom to `Custom tags must be 1 to 40 characters and use well-formed Unicode.`, reserved labels to `Custom tags cannot use a course name.`, and >10 to `Add no more than 10 custom tags.` Recipe create/edit return status 400 exact `{ errors:{ tags:<message> }, submittedTags:{ course:string, customTags:string[] } }`. Unique/limit race throws `RecipeTagConflictError` and returns 409 same shape with `Tags changed at the same time. Review and try again.` Submitted raw rows/casing are preserved; no partial write.
- Tag mutations on existing recipes use current-state declarative SQL inside one non-interactive transaction. Full replacement deletes absent custom/course rows first, inserts each desired normalized row with conflict-ignore to preserve the row/casing that exists at execution time, and then applies the recipe update. New recipe creation is the explicit exception and uses the separately required nested Prisma tag creates in its single atomic create. D1 commit order is serialization order: simultaneous full replacements may both succeed; the later commit owns complete normalized membership/course, while a normalized row retained across both commits keeps the casing/id present at the later transaction's execution. A normalized row deleted by one transaction and newly inserted by a later transaction uses that later submitted casing. There is no unowned delta add/remove API. Tests force both replacement orders, retained-overlap casing, delete/re-add casing, rollback, and injected unique/limit trigger conflicts mapped to the declared 409.
- Migration `0027_recipe_tags.sql` also creates raw-SQL singleton `SearchRebuildLease(id TEXT PRIMARY KEY CHECK(id = 'current'), lease TEXT NULL, expiresAtMs INTEGER NULL)` and conflict-ignores row `('current',NULL,NULL)`; Unit 24 applies it once and Unit 27 never rewrites it. Acquisition conditionally sets lowercase UUID and `now+60000` where null/expired and succeeds on one changed row; release matches UUID. Immediately before replacement capture one guardNowMs. Every delete/insert/metadata statement uses `lease=<uuid> AND expiresAtMs>guardNowMs`; no later clock enters the transaction, so all apply or all no-op.
- Accepted tags project exactly into SearchDocument: recipe metadata adds course plus custom display labels, body appends those labels in normalizedLabel/id order, and title/subtitle remain unchanged. RecipeTag source content hash is exact `sha256:<lowercase hex>` over UTF-8 `JSON.stringify(rows)` where rows come from active-recipe tags ordered `recipeId BINARY, kind BINARY, normalizedLabel BINARY, id BINARY` and each object has exact key order `{ id, recipeId, label, normalizedLabel, kind, source }`. The Search source fingerprint adds RecipeTag count/latestAt plus that hash; createdById/timestamps are excluded because they do not shape documents.
- One-statement structural completeness uses expected key CTE `active Recipe -> (recipe,id) UNION ALL Cookbook -> (cookbook,id) UNION ALL User -> (chef,id) UNION ALL active ShoppingListItem -> (shopping-list-item,id)` and grouped actual `(entityType,entityId)` from SearchDocument. The single returned row contains exact `expectedCount,actualRowCount,actualDistinctKeyCount,missingCount,extraCount,duplicateKeyCount,currentMetadataCount,metadataDocumentCount`. Complete means expected=actual rows=actual distinct, missing/extra/duplicate zero, currentMetadataCount one, and metadataDocumentCount=actualRowCount; query/table/type failure is incomplete. This checks key-set structure, not deliberate cached content corruption when sources are unchanged.
- Query algorithm is deterministic. Read source fingerprint plus that one-statement completeness. Complete+fresh queries immediately. Complete+stale attempts lease once at t=0; on failed acquisition because another unexpired holder exists, query old complete immediately. Incomplete attempts lease at t=0; after each failed acquisition wait exactly 25,50,100,200,400,800,1600ms, then run completeness first (query immediately if complete), then attempt lease again. After the 1600ms cycle, another failure with incomplete index throws `SearchIndexUnavailableError`; `recipes._index.tsx` and `search.tsx` return 503 text `Search is temporarily unavailable.`, v1 returns `503 service_unavailable` same message, and every MCP search operation returns retryable same text. Unit27.1 owns all consumers and response tests.
- A holder runs at most three cycles. Each cycle reads a source fingerprint, builds, executes fixed-guard atomic replacement, then reads fresh-time lease ownership, source fingerprint, and one-statement completeness in that order. Owned+matching+complete may query, then best-effort release; release failure is logged and natural 60s expiry remains, but response is valid. Source changed while still owner starts next cycle. Lost/expired lease or a failed guarded transaction becomes non-holder: if one-statement check is complete, query that old/new complete index immediately; if incomplete, follow remaining wait/acquisition schedule. After three source-change cycles, query any complete index or throw unavailable. Statement/lease/release exceptions follow the same complete-index fallback; no request queries an incomplete index. Direct REST projections remain immediate; anonymous cache policy remains.
- Discovery filters use at most one `course` and repeated `tag`. Course absent or one exact `course=` means no filter (All emits empty); one of four means filter; repeated course even empty or any other value is 400. Raw empty tag and a tag that becomes empty solely through the exact whitespace canonicalizer are ignored. Nonempty malformed-surrogate/overlength/reserved invalid tag is 400. Valid tags normalize/dedupe/sort/cap ten. Filter controls emit empty course for All and canonical display labels for tags. Search/scope/course/tags combine AND before rank/limit; unfiltered ordering stays.
- My Recipes, owner My Kitchen recipe results, and Search use one explicit GET filter form. Course is a native/menu select with `All courses` plus the four values. Custom tags are enumerated checkboxes, not free-form: options are distinct canonical CUSTOM tags on active recipes visible to that route/owner scope before q/course/tag filtering, grouped by normalizedLabel, choosing the lowest tag id's display label and sorted by normalizedLabel then id. Search shows controls for `scope=all|recipes`; supplied filters under another scope are valid but yield no non-recipe matches. `Apply filters` submits; controls never auto-submit. Forms preserve existing `q`, Search `scope`, and every unrelated query parameter as hidden fields while replacing course/tag. Removing one selected chip preserves all other parameters and tags; `Clear filters` removes only course/tag; route-level Clear Search removes q but preserves course/tag/scope. My Recipes Previous/Next links clone the current query in original pair order, preserve `q`, `course`, every repeated `tag` including its order, and every unrelated parameter, replace all existing `page` entries with one target page when target >1, and omit `page` when target is 1. At most ten boxes may be selected; the eleventh is disabled and server validation remains authoritative.
- Integrated main's My Recipes path remains bounded in SQLite. `searchMyRecipes` keeps its owner/deletedAt boundary, 50-row page size, one-row lookahead, `updatedAt DESC,id DESC` order, and existing q semantics across title/description/servings/owner username/ingredient name. Course/custom-tag predicates are added to that SQL before order/limit/offset; combined q/course/tag requests may not materialize the owner's corpus or call the legacy batched ingredient loader. Visible tag options use a separate owner-scoped pre-q/course/tag query. `test/lib/my-recipes-search.server.test.ts` and `test/routes/my-recipes-query-boundary.test.ts` are permanent regression oracles for outgoing SQL/arguments, pagination, privacy, and the no-unbounded-query boundary.
- Every task edit to `app/routes/_index.tsx` preserves integrated main's guest landing contract: the brand signal/headline/support copy remain visible, the `Collect` continuation remains inside the first viewport, the hero is at most viewport height minus 128px, the headline precedes rather than overlaps continuation content, and there is no horizontal overflow at 390x844, 1440x900, or 1920x1080. `e2e/home-hero-viewport.spec.ts` is the executable oracle and joins the final discovery visual gate plus the full release E2E run.
- Recipe create/edit forms submit exactly one `course` field (`""` means null; missing/repeated/invalid is validation error) and repeated `customTag` fields. Blank custom rows are omitted; first occurrence wins display casing; normalized duplicates collapse; parsed canonical tags sort by normalized label then submitted index. Parse/validate all fields before writes. Create uses one nested Recipe create with nested canonical tag creates. Edit passes the desired set to the current-state declarative transaction: delete rows absent from the desired normalized set, conflict-ignore desired inserts so execution-time existing ids/casing win, and apply the recipe update last. Any failure rolls back recipe and every tag change; validation returns HTTP 400 and trigger races return the exact HTTP 409 tag-conflict response with submitted course/custom rows and no partial write.
